Second Contradiction: Creation from Nothing
Second contradiction: mixture implies creation from nothing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the dualists' doctrine of mixture implies creation from nothing, which they deny.

Core Idea
Mixture arises from no prior principle, contradicting dualist rejection of creation ex nihilo.

The dualists reject that something can come from nothing, yet their concept of mixture involves a new meaning without any pre-existing source. This second contradiction highlights their inconsistency on the issue of origination.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the key phrase: 'إيجاد شيء لا من شيء' (bringing something into existence from nothing).
2
Identify what mixture is according to dualists
Mixture is a meaning (معنى) beyond the mixed entity, and it occurs from no principle (لا من أصل).
There is no prior substance that becomes mixture.
3
Recognize the contradiction
They deny origination from nothing, yet by affirming mixture, they affirm exactly that.
Thus they contradict themselves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إنهم ناقضوا في القول بالامتزاج من وجوه أحدها – أن الامتزاج بعد البينونة تغير وهو مستحيل على القديم لما هو من أمارات الحدث وثبوت أمارات الحدث في القديم محال وإثباته تناقض لما فيه من القول بالقدم والحدوث معا. والثاني - أن فيه إيجاد شيء لا من شيء وهو الامتزاج إذ هو معنى وراء الممتزج لكون الذات عندهم وقت التباين ولا امتزاج ثم هو حدث لا من أصل، إذ لا أصل للامتزاج حدث منه، وهم ينكرون حدوث الشيء لا من شيء، وقد قالوا به فتناقضوا. والثالث - أن الأصلين لما كانا متباينين ثم امتزجا فقد وجد من كل واحد من الأصلين فعلان متضادان وهما التباين والامتزاج، وهم يقولون باستحالة المتضادين من جوهر واحد، ولهذا أبوا وجود الخير والشر بفعل واحد. والرابع - أنهم ألحقوا العجز بالنور حيث زعموا أنه لا يقدر على قهر عدوه، واستنقاذ أجزائه من وثاقه، وكذا الأجزاء المحتبسة في وثاق الظلمة عاجزة عن التخلص عن قهر عدوها، وقبل الأسر كانت عاجزة عن دفع قهر الظلمة عن أنفسها، جاهلة بأسباب الدفع والتخلص، والعجز والجهل شر، وأثبتوا للظلمة قدرة على النور وأسر أجزائه، والقدرة خير وهذا هدم أصلهم وإبطال قواعد مذهبهم. والخامس أنهم يقولون: إن حركة النور علوية وحركة الظلام سفلية ثم قالوا بالامتزاج مع أنهم زعموا أن النور كان أعلى، والظلمة كانت أسفل وعند تحرك الأعلى حركة علوية والأسفل حركة سفلية يزدادان بعدا فيما بينهما لا الامتزاج، فإذا لا امتزاج إلا بتسفل العلوي أو تعلى السفلي، وكل ذلك عندهم محال فإذا أثبتوا الامتزاج مع هذا فقد ناقضوا. والسادس - أنهم جعلوا الأصلين متضادين، لأن التضاد عندهم في الجواهر دون الأعراض، فإنهم لا يقرون بثبوت الأعراض، ويقولون: إن من شأن المتضادين التنافر والتباعد ثم أثبتوا الامتزاج الذي هو الائتلاف والتقارب من غير إثبات قاهر قاهر.
Then they contradict themselves regarding the doctrine of mixture in several aspects: First—that mixture after separation is a change, and change is impossible for the eternal because it is one of the signs of origination, and the establishment of signs of origination in the eternal is impossible, and affirming it is a contradiction because it entails affirming both eternity and origination simultaneously. Second—that it involves bringing something into existence from nothing, namely mixture, for it is a meaning beyond the mixed entity, because according to them the substance at the time of separation has no mixture, then it occurs from no principle, since there is no principle from which mixture occurs, yet they deny the origination of a thing from nothing, but they have asserted it, so they contradict. Third—that since the two principles were separate and then mixed, there arise from each of the two principles two contrary acts, namely separation and mixture, yet they hold that two contraries from one substance are impossible, and for this reason they refuse that good and evil occur by one act. Fourth—that they attribute impotence to light, claiming that it cannot overcome its enemy or rescue its parts from its bonds, and likewise the parts imprisoned in the bonds of darkness are unable to free themselves from their enemy's domination, and before capture they were unable to repel the domination of darkness from themselves, ignorant of the means of repulsion and escape, and impotence and ignorance are evil. Yet they attribute power to darkness over light and the capture of its parts, and power is good—this demolishes their foundation and invalidates the principles of their school. Fifth—that they say the motion of light is upward and the motion of darkness is downward, then they affirm mixture, even though they claim that light was above and darkness below, and when the higher moves with an upward motion and the lower with a downward motion, they become more distant from each other, not mixed. So mixture occurs only by the higher descending or the lower ascending, and all that is impossible according to them—so if they affirm mixture despite this, they contradict. Sixth—that they made the two principles opposites, because according to them opposition is in substances, not in accidents (for they do not affirm the subsistence of accidents), and they say that the nature of opposites is to repel and separate. Then they affirm mixture, which is harmony and proximity, without positing an overpowering overcomer.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of six contradictions (وجوه) that dualists fall into regarding their doctrine of mixture (امتزاج) of light and darkness. Each point is a self-contained argument showing inconsistency.

1. First contradiction: Mixture after separation is a change, which is a sign of origination. Since they claim light and darkness are eternal, change in them is impossible. So affirming mixture while claiming eternality is contradictory.

2. Second contradiction: Mixture is a new meaning with no prior principle, i.e., it comes from nothing. But they deny creation from nothing, yet they affirm mixture, so they contradict.

3. Third contradiction: From each principle (light and darkness) two opposite acts proceed (separation and mixture), but they hold that two contraries cannot issue from one substance. Moreover, they use this to deny that good and evil come from one agent, yet they themselves attribute opposite acts to each principle.

4. Fourth contradiction: They attribute impotence and ignorance (evils) to light, but power (good) to darkness. This violates their own principle that the source of good (light) should not produce evil and vice versa.

5. Fifth contradiction: Light's motion is upward, darkness's motion is downward. If they move in their natural directions, they move apart, not together. Mixture would require one to move against its nature, which they deem impossible. So affirming mixture contradicts their own physics.

6. Sixth contradiction: They hold that opposition is in substances and that opposites repel and separate. Yet they affirm mixture (harmony and proximity) of these two opposite substances without any external overcomer, which is inconsistent.

Key Terms
الامتزاج
القديم
الحادث
لا من شيء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the dualist doctrine of mixture imply according to the second contradiction?
A) Mixture is a combination of pre-existing parts
B) Mixture is a new meaning with no prior source
C) Mixture is eternal
D) Mixture is an accident

Key Takeaway
The dualists' denial of creation ex nihilo is contradicted by their own concept of mixture, which requires exactly that.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The dualists denied creation from nothing but their own theory demanded it. In your life, do you ever deny Allah’s sole creative power in certain areas (e.g., attributing success to your own skill alone) while acting as if He creates? Can you identify one specific habit where you need to realign your belief with your actions, and commit to changing it this week?
?
The argument hinges on the absence of a principle (أصل) for mixture. Think of a recent event you dismissed as 'coincidence' or 'random'. Do you truly believe there is no cause? As a Muslim, how does this lesson push you to see everything as created by Allah, even when you cannot see the cause? What practical difference would this make in your daily reliance on Him?

Third Contradiction: Two Contraries from One Substance
Third contradiction: each principle would produce contrary acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why attributing both separation and mixture to a single principle violates the dualist principle that one substance cannot produce two contrary acts.

Core Idea
Each principle would have to produce opposite acts, which dualists themselves deem impossible.

The dualists hold that a single substance cannot be the source of two contrary acts, yet their doctrine of mixture requires that each of the two principles (light and darkness) produce both separation and mixture. This third contradiction exposes an inconsistency in their causal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Focus on the terms 'فعلان متضادان' (two contrary acts).
2
Identify the two acts
Separation (التباين) and mixture (الامتزاج) are contrary acts.
3
Understand the dualist principle
They hold that two contraries cannot proceed from one substance (جوهر واحد).
They use this to deny that good and evil come from one agent.
4
Apply to their own doctrine
Each principle (light and darkness) is one substance, yet would have to produce both separation and mixture. This violates their own principle.
Hence a contradiction.

Source Text

What is the dualist principle that the third contradiction uses against them?
A) Opposites attract

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever hold beliefs about Allah that contradict each other? Take a moment to identify one area where your understanding might be inconsistent—and commit to resolving it by seeking knowledge.
?
This argument exposes that falsehood eventually collapses under its own logic. What assumption have you made about your faith that, if honestly examined, might turn out to be based on a shaky foundation? Will you test it today?
?
If you truly believe that only one God can be the source of both good and evil, how does that change the way you face hardship? Are you willing to trust Him completely—even in trials that seem to come from a 'dark' source?

Fourth Contradiction: Attributing Evil to Light and Good to Darkness
Fourth contradiction: evil attributed to light, good to darkness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the dualists' attributions of impotence to light and power to darkness undermine their fundamental classification of good and evil.

Core Idea
They attribute evil (impotence, ignorance) to light and good (power) to darkness, reversing their own principles.

Dualists believe light is the source of good and darkness the source of evil. Yet in their account of mixture, light is impotent and ignorant (evil attributes), while darkness has power (good attribute). This fourth contradiction shows how their narrative violates their own foundational categories.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the opposite attributions: light is called 'عاجز' (impotent) and 'جاهل' (ignorant); darkness has 'قدرة' (power).
2
Recall dualist axioms
Light is the principle of good; darkness is the principle of evil. Evil includes impotence and ignorance; good includes power and knowledge.
3
Identify the inversion
In the story of mixture, light is weak and ignorant (evil), while darkness is strong (good). This contradicts their axioms.
4
See the conclusion
The author says this demolishes their foundation and invalidates their school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary

Checkpoint
According to the fourth contradiction, what evil traits are attributed to light in the dualist narrative?
A) Power and knowledge
B) Impotence and ignorance
C) Motion and rest
D) Separation and mixture

Key Takeaway
The dualists' own story contradicts their moral classification by ascribing evil to light and good to darkness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The dualists claimed light is good yet described it as weak and ignorant. Where in your own life do you claim to trust Allah's power but act as if you are helpless or ignorant? Will you repent of that inconsistency today?
?
They attributed power to darkness—something they considered evil. Are there any 'dark' habits or desires you secretly rely on for strength? What would it mean to instead derive all your power from Allah alone?
?
If you truly believe that all good comes from Allah, do your thoughts and actions reflect that reliance, or do you sometimes credit other sources? Commit to one specific change to align your belief with your practice.

Fifth Contradiction: Natural Motions Prevent Mixture
Fifth contradiction: natural motions prevent mixture.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the dualists' physics of upward and downward motion makes mixture impossible without violating natural tendencies.

Core Idea
If light moves up and darkness moves down, they move apart; mixture requires one to move against its nature.

Dualists hold that light's natural motion is upward and darkness's motion is downward. If they move in their natural directions, they become more distant, not mixed. For mixture to occur, one must move against its nature, which they consider impossible. This fifth contradiction highlights an internal inconsistency in their cosmology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the claims about motion: حركة النور علوية وحركة الظلام سفلية.
2
Understand natural motions
Light moves upward, darkness moves downward by nature.
3
Analyze the consequence
If each moves in its natural direction, they separate further, not mix.
4
Identify the impossible prerequisite
Mixture would require one to move opposite to its nature (e.g., light descending or darkness ascending).
Dualists deem such movement impossible.
5
Contradiction
They affirm mixture while denying the necessary conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إنهم ناقضوا في القول بالامتزاج من وجوه أحدها – أن الامتزاج بعد البينونة تغير وهو مستحيل على القديم لما هو من أمارات الحدث وثبوت أمارات الحدث في القديم محال وإثباته تناقض لما فيه من القول بالقدم والحدوث معا. والثاني - أن فيه إيجاد شيء لا من شيء وهو الامتزاج إذ هو معنى وراء الممتزج لكون الذات عندهم وقت التباين ولا امتزاج ثم هو حدث لا من أصل، إذ لا أصل للامتزاج حدث منه، وهم ينكرون حدوث الشيء لا من شيء، وقد قالوا به فتناقضوا. والثالث - أن الأصلين لما كانا متباينين ثم امتزجا فقد وجد من كل واحد من الأصلين فعلان متضادان وهما التباين والامتزاج، وهم يقولون باستحالة المتضادين من جوهر واحد، ولهذا أبوا وجود الخير والشر بفعل واحد. والرابع - أنهم ألحقوا العجز بالنور حيث زعموا أنه لا يقدر على قهر عدوه، واستنقاذ أجزائه من وثاقه، وكذا الأجزاء المحتبسة في وثاق الظلمة عاجزة عن التخلص عن قهر عدوها، وقبل الأسر كانت عاجزة عن دفع قهر الظلمة عن أنفسها، جاهلة بأسباب الدفع والتخلص، والعجز والجهل شر، وأثبتوا للظلمة قدرة على النور وأسر أجزائه، والقدرة خير وهذا هدم أصلهم وإبطال قواعد مذهبهم. والخامس أنهم يقولون: إن حركة النور علوية وحركة الظلام سفلية ثم قالوا بالامتزاج مع أنهم زعموا أن النور كان أعلى، والظلمة كانت أسفل وعند تحرك الأعلى حركة علوية والأسفل حركة سفلية يزدادان بعدا فيما بينهما لا الامتزاج، فإذا لا امتزاج إلا بتسفل العلوي أو تعلى السفلي، وكل ذلك عندهم محال فإذا أثبتوا الامتزاج مع هذا فقد ناقضوا. والسادس - أنهم جعلوا الأصلين متضادين، لأن التضاد عندهم في الجواهر دون الأعراض، فإنهم لا يقرون بثبوت الأعراض، ويقولون: إن من شأن المتضادين التنافر والتباعد ثم أثبتوا الامتزاج الذي هو الائتلاف والتقارب من غير إثبات قاهر قاهر.
Then they contradict themselves regarding the doctrine of mixture in several aspects: First—that mixture after separation is a change, and change is impossible for the eternal because it is one of the signs of origination, and the establishment of signs of origination in the eternal is impossible, and affirming it is a contradiction because it entails affirming both eternity and origination simultaneously. Second—that it involves bringing something into existence from nothing, namely mixture, for it is a meaning beyond the mixed entity, because according to them the substance at the time of separation has no mixture, then it occurs from no principle, since there is no principle from which mixture occurs, yet they deny the origination of a thing from nothing, but they have asserted it, so they contradict. Third—that since the two principles were separate and then mixed, there arise from each of the two principles two contrary acts, namely separation and mixture, yet they hold that two contraries from one substance are impossible, and for this reason they refuse that good and evil occur by one act. Fourth—that they attribute impotence to light, claiming that it cannot overcome its enemy or rescue its parts from its bonds, and likewise the parts imprisoned in the bonds of darkness are unable to free themselves from their enemy's domination, and before capture they were unable to repel the domination of darkness from themselves, ignorant of the means of repulsion and escape, and impotence and ignorance are evil. Yet they attribute power to darkness over light and the capture of its parts, and power is good—this demolishes their foundation and invalidates the principles of their school. Fifth—that they say the motion of light is upward and the motion of darkness is downward, then they affirm mixture, even though they claim that light was above and darkness below, and when the higher moves with an upward motion and the lower with a downward motion, they become more distant from each other, not mixed. So mixture occurs only by the higher descending or the lower ascending, and all that is impossible according to them—so if they affirm mixture despite this, they contradict. Sixth—that they made the two principles opposites, because according to them opposition is in substances, not in accidents (for they do not affirm the subsistence of accidents), and they say that the nature of opposites is to repel and separate. Then they affirm mixture, which is harmony and proximity, without positing an overpowering overcomer.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of six contradictions (وجوه) that dualists fall into regarding their doctrine of mixture (امتزاج) of light and darkness. Each point is a self-contained argument showing inconsistency.

1. First contradiction: Mixture after separation is a change, which is a sign of origination. Since they claim light and darkness are eternal, change in them is impossible. So affirming mixture while claiming eternality is contradictory.

2. Second contradiction: Mixture is a new meaning with no prior principle, i.e., it comes from nothing. But they deny creation from nothing, yet they affirm mixture, so they contradict.

3. Third contradiction: From each principle (light and darkness) two opposite acts proceed (separation and mixture), but they hold that two contraries cannot issue from one substance. Moreover, they use this to deny that good and evil come from one agent, yet they themselves attribute opposite acts to each principle.

4. Fourth contradiction: They attribute impotence and ignorance (evils) to light, but power (good) to darkness. This violates their own principle that the source of good (light) should not produce evil and vice versa.

5. Fifth contradiction: Light's motion is upward, darkness's motion is downward. If they move in their natural directions, they move apart, not together. Mixture would require one to move against its nature, which they deem impossible. So affirming mixture contradicts their own physics.

6. Sixth contradiction: They hold that opposition is in substances and that opposites repel and separate. Yet they affirm mixture (harmony and proximity) of these two opposite substances without any external overcomer, which is inconsistent.

Key Terms
النور
الظلمة
حركة علوية
حركة سفلية
الامتزاج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the dualists' doctrine of natural motions make mixture impossible?
A) Because light and darkness are both immovable
B) Because their natural motions take them apart, not together
C) Because mixture requires rest, not motion
D) Because they have no motions at all

Key Takeaway
The dualist physics of natural motion precludes mixture unless one principle acts against its nature, which they deem impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own life, are there beliefs or actions that contradict each other, like the dualists affirming mixture while denying the means? Take a moment to identify one area where your practice does not align with your profession of tawheed. What step will you take today to resolve that inconsistency?
?
The dualists assumed that light and darkness have fixed natures that cannot change. Do you ever assume that your own habits or sins are 'fixed' and cannot be changed, even though you believe Allah has power over all things? How does reflecting on Allah's absolute power challenge your excuses for remaining the same?
?
If you were to examine the foundations of your faith honestly, do you rely on any secondary causes as if they act independently, while affirming that Allah alone is the Creator and Sustainer? What would it mean for you to live out the reality that nothing happens except by His will and power?

4 min
Sixth Contradiction: Opposites Repel, but Mixture Requires Harmony
Sixth contradiction: opposites repel, mixture requires harmony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the dualist view of opposites as naturally repelling contradicts the possibility of mixture without a compelling force.

Core Idea
Opposites repel and separate by nature, so mixture requires an external overcomer, which dualists do not posit.

Dualists define light and darkness as opposites and hold that opposites by nature repel and separate. Yet they affirm mixture, which is harmony and proximity. This sixth contradiction shows that without any external force to overcome their natural repulsion, mixture is inconsistent with their own definition of opposites.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Focus on the terms 'متضادين' (opposites) and 'التنافر والتباعد' (repulsion and separation).
2
Understand dualist view of opposition
Opposition exists in substances, not accidents. The nature of opposites is to repel and separate.
They deny accidents.
3
Apply to light and darkness
Light and darkness are opposite substances, so they naturally repel.
4
Contradiction with mixture
Mixture is harmony (ائتلاف) and proximity (تقارب), opposite to repulsion.
They affirm mixture without any external overcomer (قاهر).
5
Identify the missing element
For opposites to mix, there must be an external force to override their natural repulsion. They provide none.
Thus contradiction.

Argument 2: Mixture as Creation from Nothing
Second objection: mixture as something from nothing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the dualists' acceptance of mixture implies creation from nothing, contradicting their own denial of creatio ex nihilo.

Core Idea
Mixture comes from nothing, so dualists contradict themselves.

The second argument targets the dualist claim that light and darkness mix. Al-Nasafi points out that mixture is a new entity arising from no prior material—precisely what the dualists deny. This contradiction undermines their position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Note the logical structure: premise, implication, contradiction.
The argument is concise; each part builds on the previous.
2
Understand 'mixture' as a new entity
The dualists treat mixture as a reality distinct from the mixed elements. It arises at the time of separation, yet it has no prior origin.
3
Identify the contradiction
The dualists deny creation from nothing, but in affirming mixture they admit something from nothing. This is a direct self-contradiction.
The conclusion 'they contradict themselves' is explicit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني - أن فيه إيجاد شيء لا من شيء وهو الامتزاج إذ هو معنى وراء الممتزج لكون الذات عندهم وقت التباين ولا امتزاج ثم هو حدث لا من أصل، إذ لا أصل للامتزاج حدث منه، وهم ينكرون حدوث الشيء لا من شيء، وقد قالوا به فتناقضوا. والثالث - أن الأصلين لما كانا متباينين ثم امتزجا فقد وجد من كل واحد من الأصلين فعلان متضادان وهما التباين والامتزاج، وهم يقولون باستحالة المتضادين من جوهر واحد ، ولهذا أبوا وجود الخير والشر بفعل واحد. والرابع - أنهم ألحقوا العجز بالنور حيث زعموا أنه لا يقدر على قهر عدوه، واستنقاذ أجزائه من وثاقه، وكذا الأجزاء المحتبسة فى وثاق الظلمة عاجزة عن التخلص عن قهر عدوها، وقبل الأسر كانت عاجزة عن دفع قهر الظلمة عن أنفسها، جاهلة بأسباب الدفع، والتخلص، والعجز والجهل شر ، وأثبتوا للظلمة قدرة على النور وأسر أجزائه، والقدرة خير وهذا هدم أصلهم وإبطال قواعد مذهبهم. والخامس أنهم يقولون : إن حركة النور علوية وحركة الظلام سفلية ثم قالوا بالامتزاج مع أنهم زعموا أن النور كان أعلى، والظلمة كانت أسفل وعند تحرك الأعلى حركة علوية والأسفل حركة سفلية يزدادان بعدا فيما بينهما لا الامتزاج، فإذا لا امتزاج إلا بتسفل العلوي أو تعلى السفلي، وكل ذلك عندهم محال فإذا أثبتوا الامتزاج مع هذا فقد ناقضوا. والسادس - أنهم جعلوا الأصلين متضادين، لأن التضاد عندهم في الجواهر دون الأعراض، فإنهم لا يقرون بثبوت الأعراض، ويقولون : إن من شأن المتضادين التنافر والتباعد ثم أثبتوا الامتزاج الذي هو الائتلاف والتقارب من غير إثبات قهر قاهر عليهما بل بأنفسهما وطباعهما، وهذا تناقض ظاهر ، والحمد لله على التوفيق.
The second [argument] - that in it there is bringing into existence something from nothing, that is mixture (al-imitizāj), since it is a meaning beyond the mixed, because the essence at the time of separation (al-tabāyun) has no mixture. Then it is an occurrence from no origin, since there is no origin for mixture from which it occurs, and they deny the occurrence of something from nothing, yet they have said it, so they contradict themselves. The third - that since the two principles were separated, then they mixed, from each of the two principles there came to be two contradictory acts, which are separation and mixture, and they say the impossibility of two contradictories from a single substance (jawhar), and for this they refused the existence of good and evil by a single act. The fourth - that they attributed weakness (al-‘ajz) to light, claiming that it cannot subdue its enemy and rescue its parts from its bonds, and likewise the parts confined in the bonds of darkness are incapable of freeing themselves from the force of their enemy, and before captivity they were incapable of repelling the force of darkness from themselves, ignorant of the means of repulsion and liberation, and weakness and ignorance are evil, and they affirmed for darkness power over light and the captivity of its parts, and power is good, and this demolishes their principle and invalidates the foundations of their doctrine. The fifth - that they say: the motion of light is upward and the motion of darkness is downward, then they affirmed mixture despite their claim that light was above and darkness below, and when the higher moves upward and the lower moves downward, they increase distance between them, not mixture. Thus mixture occurs only by the higher moving down or the lower moving up, and all that is impossible according to them. So if they affirm mixture with this, they have contradicted themselves. The sixth - that they made the two principles opposites, because opposition (al-taḍād) according to them is in substances (al-jawāhir) not accidents (al-a‘rāḍ), for they do not affirm the existence of accidents, and they say: it is the nature of opposites to repel and separate. Then they affirmed mixture, which is harmony and proximity, without affirming any compelling force over them, but rather by themselves and their natures, and this is a manifest contradiction, and praise be to God for success.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage presents six arguments against the dualists, who believe in two eternal principles: light (good) and darkness (evil). Each objection aims to show that the dualists' own principles lead to contradictions when applied to their doctrine of mixture (imitizāj) between light and darkness. The second argument points out that mixture is something new coming from no prior material, yet the dualists deny creation from nothing. The third argues that if two separated principles mix, each would produce two contradictory acts (separation and mixture) from a single substance, which they deem impossible. The fourth notes that they attribute weakness and ignorance (evils) to light but power (good) to darkness, contradicting their own assignment of good to light. The fifth uses the claims about upward/downward motion to show mixture would require impossible movements. The sixth notes that they consider opposites inherently repellent, yet mixture implies harmony, which they claim without a compelling force. The author concludes each objection with 'thus they contradict themselves.'

Key Terms
الامتزاج (al-imitizāj)
التباين (al-tabāyun)
أصل (aṣl)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Mixture is just a mechanical combination of pre-existing parts.
Correction: The dualists treat mixture as a new, independent reality, not a mere rearrangement. Hence it must be created ex nihilo.

Checkpoint
What does the dualists' acceptance of mixture necessarily imply according to the second argument?
A) Creation from nothing
B) Eternal pre-existence
C) Accidental property
D) Impossibility of separation

Key Takeaway
The dualists' affirmation of mixture forces them to accept creation from nothing, contradicting their own denial.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The dualists were logically inconsistent—they accepted mixture even though it implied creation from nothing. Where in your own life do you hold contradictory beliefs? This week, identify one area where your actions contradict what you profess to believe about Allah's power, and resolve to align them.
?
If mixture arises from nothing, then everything you have—your health, wealth, relationships—also comes from nothing by Allah's will. Have you truly thanked Him for creating these from nothing just for you? What keeps you from feeling that gratitude daily?
?
The dualists' error was denying a truth that their own system forced them to accept. Are there truths about Allah that you know in your mind but resist accepting in your heart? Commit to one such truth today and act on it.

Argument 3: Contradictory Acts from One Substance
Third objection: contradictory acts from each principle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the dualist view of mixture leads to the impossibility of two contradictory acts from a single substance.

Core Idea
Two contradictory acts cannot come from one substance.

The third argument uses the dualists' own principle that two contradictory acts cannot arise from a single substance. If light and darkness were separated and then mix, each principle would produce both separation and mixture—two opposites from one source.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument
Read the Arabic and translation. Identify the two acts: separation (tabāyun) and mixture (imitizāj).
2
Understand the principle quoted from dualists
The dualists hold that two contradictory acts cannot come from a single substance (jawhar wāḥid). They use this to deny that good and evil can come from one source.
This is a key premise.
3
Apply to light and darkness
If each principle was originally separate and then mixes, each would have both separation and mixture—contradictory acts. This violates their own rule.
The conclusion is that they contradict themselves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني - أن فيه إيجاد شيء لا من شيء وهو الامتزاج إذ هو معنى وراء الممتزج لكون الذات عندهم وقت التباين ولا امتزاج ثم هو حدث لا من أصل، إذ لا أصل للامتزاج حدث منه، وهم ينكرون حدوث الشيء لا من شيء، وقد قالوا به فتناقضوا. والثالث - أن الأصلين لما كانا متباينين ثم امتزجا فقد وجد من كل واحد من الأصلين فعلان متضادان وهما التباين والامتزاج، وهم يقولون باستحالة المتضادين من جوهر واحد ، ولهذا أبوا وجود الخير والشر بفعل واحد. والرابع - أنهم ألحقوا العجز بالنور حيث زعموا أنه لا يقدر على قهر عدوه، واستنقاذ أجزائه من وثاقه، وكذا الأجزاء المحتبسة فى وثاق الظلمة عاجزة عن التخلص عن قهر عدوها، وقبل الأسر كانت عاجزة عن دفع قهر الظلمة عن أنفسها، جاهلة بأسباب الدفع، والتخلص، والعجز والجهل شر ، وأثبتوا للظلمة قدرة على النور وأسر أجزائه، والقدرة خير وهذا هدم أصلهم وإبطال قواعد مذهبهم. والخامس أنهم يقولون : إن حركة النور علوية وحركة الظلام سفلية ثم قالوا بالامتزاج مع أنهم زعموا أن النور كان أعلى، والظلمة كانت أسفل وعند تحرك الأعلى حركة علوية والأسفل حركة سفلية يزدادان بعدا فيما بينهما لا الامتزاج، فإذا لا امتزاج إلا بتسفل العلوي أو تعلى السفلي، وكل ذلك عندهم محال فإذا أثبتوا الامتزاج مع هذا فقد ناقضوا. والسادس - أنهم جعلوا الأصلين متضادين، لأن التضاد عندهم في الجواهر دون الأعراض، فإنهم لا يقرون بثبوت الأعراض، ويقولون : إن من شأن المتضادين التنافر والتباعد ثم أثبتوا الامتزاج الذي هو الائتلاف والتقارب من غير إثبات قهر قاهر عليهما بل بأنفسهما وطباعهما، وهذا تناقض ظاهر ، والحمد لله على التوفيق.
The second [argument] - that in it there is bringing into existence something from nothing, that is mixture (al-imitizāj), since it is a meaning beyond the mixed, because the essence at the time of separation (al-tabāyun) has no mixture. Then it is an occurrence from no origin, since there is no origin for mixture from which it occurs, and they deny the occurrence of something from nothing, yet they have said it, so they contradict themselves. The third - that since the two principles were separated, then they mixed, from each of the two principles there came to be two contradictory acts, which are separation and mixture, and they say the impossibility of two contradictories from a single substance (jawhar), and for this they refused the existence of good and evil by a single act. The fourth - that they attributed weakness (al-‘ajz) to light, claiming that it cannot subdue its enemy and rescue its parts from its bonds, and likewise the parts confined in the bonds of darkness are incapable of freeing themselves from the force of their enemy, and before captivity they were incapable of repelling the force of darkness from themselves, ignorant of the means of repulsion and liberation, and weakness and ignorance are evil, and they affirmed for darkness power over light and the captivity of its parts, and power is good, and this demolishes their principle and invalidates the foundations of their doctrine. The fifth - that they say: the motion of light is upward and the motion of darkness is downward, then they affirmed mixture despite their claim that light was above and darkness below, and when the higher moves upward and the lower moves downward, they increase distance between them, not mixture. Thus mixture occurs only by the higher moving down or the lower moving up, and all that is impossible according to them. So if they affirm mixture with this, they have contradicted themselves. The sixth - that they made the two principles opposites, because opposition (al-taḍād) according to them is in substances (al-jawāhir) not accidents (al-a‘rāḍ), for they do not affirm the existence of accidents, and they say: it is the nature of opposites to repel and separate. Then they affirmed mixture, which is harmony and proximity, without affirming any compelling force over them, but rather by themselves and their natures, and this is a manifest contradiction, and praise be to God for success.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage presents six arguments against the dualists, who believe in two eternal principles: light (good) and darkness (evil). Each objection aims to show that the dualists' own principles lead to contradictions when applied to their doctrine of mixture (imitizāj) between light and darkness. The second argument points out that mixture is something new coming from no prior material, yet the dualists deny creation from nothing. The third argues that if two separated principles mix, each would produce two contradictory acts (separation and mixture) from a single substance, which they deem impossible. The fourth notes that they attribute weakness and ignorance (evils) to light but power (good) to darkness, contradicting their own assignment of good to light. The fifth uses the claims about upward/downward motion to show mixture would require impossible movements. The sixth notes that they consider opposites inherently repellent, yet mixture implies harmony, which they claim without a compelling force. The author concludes each objection with 'thus they contradict themselves.'

Key Terms
فعلان متضادان (fiʿlān mutaḍāddān)
جوهر واحد (jawhar wāḥid)
التباين (al-tabāyun)
الامتزاج (al-imitizāj)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What do the dualists consider impossible for a single substance?
A) Having two contradictory acts
B) Having one act
C) Mixing with another substance
D) Being eternal

Key Takeaway
The dualists' own rule against contradictory acts from one substance is violated by their doctrine of mixture.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself attributing your good deeds to your own effort and your bad deeds to circumstances or shaytan, as if two different sources produced them? How does this lesson challenge you to take ownership of all your actions before Allah?
?
The dualists insisted on two principles to avoid contradiction. But you believe in one God who decrees both good and evil. Are you fully content with this belief, or do you secretly wish to assign the hard parts of life to a separate source? What would it change in your prayer life if you truly internalized that all acts are from one Lord?
?
Consider your own heart: do you try to keep parts of your life separate—your 'spiritual' self and your 'worldly' self—as if they come from different principles? What one step can you take today to unify your life under the single command of Allah?

Argument 4: Attributing Weakness to Light and Power to Darkness
Fourth objection: reversal of good and evil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will see how the dualist account inverts the moral qualities of good and evil, attributing weakness (evil) to light and power (good) to darkness.

Core Idea
Dualists attribute evil to light and good to darkness, reversing their own tenets.

The fourth argument focuses on the moral implications of the dualist narrative. Al-Nasafi points out that they describe light as weak and ignorant (evils) and darkness as powerful (good), which contradicts their identification of light with good and darkness with evil.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the description of light as weak and ignorant, and darkness as powerful.
2
Identify the attributes
The passage lists: weakness (ʿajz), ignorance (jahl) for light; power (qudra) for darkness. These are moral qualities.
3
Compare with dualist principles
Dualists hold that light is good and darkness is evil. Yet here they attribute evil (weakness, ignorance) to light and good (power) to darkness. This is a direct contradiction.
The conclusion: it demolishes their own foundations.

Misconception: The dualist story consistently identifies light with good and darkness with evil.

According to the fourth argument, what do the dualists attribute to light?
A) Power and knowledge
B) Weakness and ignorance
C) Mixture and separation
D) Upward motion

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Where in your life do you claim to love goodness but actually treat it as weak—hesitating to speak truth, defend justice, or act on what you know is right?
?
Have you ever relied on something you consider 'evil' (like manipulation or pride) because it seemed powerful, while neglecting the quiet power of truth and humility? What would it take for you to reverse that today?
?
If you truly believe that weakness and ignorance are evil and power is good, then where are you excusing your own weakness and ignorance, and where are you crediting yourself with power that actually comes from darkness? Name one area and commit to one change.

Argument 5: Contradiction in Motion and Mixture
Fifth objection: motion incompatibility with mixture

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the dualist claims about the natural motions of light and darkness make mixture impossible.

Core Idea
Upward and downward motions prevent mixture, not cause it.

The fifth argument addresses the dualist belief that light moves upward and darkness downward. Al-Nasafi argues that if they move in opposite directions, they would only separate further, never mix. Mixture would require light to descend or darkness to ascend, which dualists consider impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the claims about motion: light upward, darkness downward.
2
Understand the logical outcome
If light moves upward and darkness downward, they move away from each other. Mixture would require the opposite: light descending or darkness ascending.
3
Identify the contradiction
The dualists affirm mixture despite their own motion principles. Mixture is only possible through motions they deem impossible. Hence, they contradict themselves.
The conclusion is explicit: 'they have contradicted themselves'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني - أن فيه إيجاد شيء لا من شيء وهو الامتزاج إذ هو معنى وراء الممتزج لكون الذات عندهم وقت التباين ولا امتزاج ثم هو حدث لا من أصل، إذ لا أصل للامتزاج حدث منه، وهم ينكرون حدوث الشيء لا من شيء، وقد قالوا به فتناقضوا. والثالث - أن الأصلين لما كانا متباينين ثم امتزجا فقد وجد من كل واحد من الأصلين فعلان متضادان وهما التباين والامتزاج، وهم يقولون باستحالة المتضادين من جوهر واحد ، ولهذا أبوا وجود الخير والشر بفعل واحد. والرابع - أنهم ألحقوا العجز بالنور حيث زعموا أنه لا يقدر على قهر عدوه، واستنقاذ أجزائه من وثاقه، وكذا الأجزاء المحتبسة فى وثاق الظلمة عاجزة عن التخلص عن قهر عدوها، وقبل الأسر كانت عاجزة عن دفع قهر الظلمة عن أنفسها، جاهلة بأسباب الدفع، والتخلص، والعجز والجهل شر ، وأثبتوا للظلمة قدرة على النور وأسر أجزائه، والقدرة خير وهذا هدم أصلهم وإبطال قواعد مذهبهم. والخامس أنهم يقولون : إن حركة النور علوية وحركة الظلام سفلية ثم قالوا بالامتزاج مع أنهم زعموا أن النور كان أعلى، والظلمة كانت أسفل وعند تحرك الأعلى حركة علوية والأسفل حركة سفلية يزدادان بعدا فيما بينهما لا الامتزاج، فإذا لا امتزاج إلا بتسفل العلوي أو تعلى السفلي، وكل ذلك عندهم محال فإذا أثبتوا الامتزاج مع هذا فقد ناقضوا. والسادس - أنهم جعلوا الأصلين متضادين، لأن التضاد عندهم في الجواهر دون الأعراض، فإنهم لا يقرون بثبوت الأعراض، ويقولون : إن من شأن المتضادين التنافر والتباعد ثم أثبتوا الامتزاج الذي هو الائتلاف والتقارب من غير إثبات قهر قاهر عليهما بل بأنفسهما وطباعهما، وهذا تناقض ظاهر ، والحمد لله على التوفيق.

What must occur for mixture to happen, according to the fifth argument?
A) Light moves downward or darkness moves upward
B) Light and darkness move in parallel

D) Darkness moves downward only

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The dualists held two beliefs that logically contradict. Are there any beliefs you hold about God or the universe that, upon honest examination, might conflict? Will you examine them this week?
?
This argument shows that even 'natural' assumptions can lead to self-contradiction. When was the last time you changed a deeply held belief because you found it inconsistent? If not, what holds you back?
?
The dualists refused to let go of either claim, leading to inconsistency. Is there an area in your life where you cling to two opposing ideas—perhaps about your own identity, God's mercy, or His justice—out of comfort rather than truth? What step will you take to resolve it?

Argument 6: Mixture of Opposites Without a Compelling Force
Sixth objection: mixture of opposites without a compeller

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the dualist claim that opposites naturally repel makes mixture impossible without an external force.

Core Idea
Opposites repel; mixture requires a compelling force, which dualists deny.

The sixth argument targets the dualist view of opposites. They believe light and darkness are opposites, which naturally repel and avoid each other. Yet they affirm mixture, which is harmony and proximity. Al-Nasafi argues that mixture without a compelling force (qāhir) contradicts their own principle that opposites repel by nature.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Focus on the definition of opposites (taḍād) and their natural tendency to repel.
2
Understand the dualist position on opposites
Dualists hold that opposition exists only in substances, not accidents, and that opposites naturally repel (tanāfur wa tabāʿud).
3
Identify the contradiction
Mixture is the opposite of repulsion: it is harmony (iʾtilāf) and proximity (taqārub). The dualists say that mixture occurs by themselves without any external force. This goes against the nature of opposites.
The conclusion: 'this is a manifest contradiction'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني - أن فيه إيجاد شيء لا من شيء وهو الامتزاج إذ هو معنى وراء الممتزج لكون الذات عندهم وقت التباين ولا امتزاج ثم هو حدث لا من أصل، إذ لا أصل للامتزاج حدث منه، وهم ينكرون حدوث الشيء لا من شيء، وقد قالوا به فتناقضوا. والثالث - أن الأصلين لما كانا متباينين ثم امتزجا فقد وجد من كل واحد من الأصلين فعلان متضادان وهما التباين والامتزاج، وهم يقولون باستحالة المتضادين من جوهر واحد ، ولهذا أبوا وجود الخير والشر بفعل واحد. والرابع - أنهم ألحقوا العجز بالنور حيث زعموا أنه لا يقدر على قهر عدوه، واستنقاذ أجزائه من وثاقه، وكذا الأجزاء المحتبسة فى وثاق الظلمة عاجزة عن التخلص عن قهر عدوها، وقبل الأسر كانت عاجزة عن دفع قهر الظلمة عن أنفسها، جاهلة بأسباب الدفع، والتخلص، والعجز والجهل شر ، وأثبتوا للظلمة قدرة على النور وأسر أجزائه، والقدرة خير وهذا هدم أصلهم وإبطال قواعد مذهبهم. والخامس أنهم يقولون : إن حركة النور علوية وحركة الظلام سفلية ثم قالوا بالامتزاج مع أنهم زعموا أن النور كان أعلى، والظلمة كانت أسفل وعند تحرك الأعلى حركة علوية والأسفل حركة سفلية يزدادان بعدا فيما بينهما لا الامتزاج، فإذا لا امتزاج إلا بتسفل العلوي أو تعلى السفلي، وكل ذلك عندهم محال فإذا أثبتوا الامتزاج مع هذا فقد ناقضوا. والسادس - أنهم جعلوا الأصلين متضادين، لأن التضاد عندهم في الجواهر دون الأعراض، فإنهم لا يقرون بثبوت الأعراض، ويقولون : إن من شأن المتضادين التنافر والتباعد ثم أثبتوا الامتزاج الذي هو الائتلاف والتقارب من غير إثبات قهر قاهر عليهما بل بأنفسهما وطباعهما، وهذا تناقض ظاهر ، والحمد لله على التوفيق.
The second [argument] - that in it there is bringing into existence something from nothing, that is mixture (al-imitizāj), since it is a meaning beyond the mixed, because the essence at the time of separation (al-tabāyun) has no mixture. Then it is an occurrence from no origin, since there is no origin for mixture from which it occurs, and they deny the occurrence of something from nothing, yet they have said it, so they contradict themselves. The third - that since the two principles were separated, then they mixed, from each of the two principles there came to be two contradictory acts, which are separation and mixture, and they say the impossibility of two contradictories from a single substance (jawhar), and for this they refused the existence of good and evil by a single act. The fourth - that they attributed weakness (al-‘ajz) to light, claiming that it cannot subdue its enemy and rescue its parts from its bonds, and likewise the parts confined in the bonds of darkness are incapable of freeing themselves from the force of their enemy, and before captivity they were incapable of repelling the force of darkness from themselves, ignorant of the means of repulsion and liberation, and weakness and ignorance are evil, and they affirmed for darkness power over light and the captivity of its parts, and power is good, and this demolishes their principle and invalidates the foundations of their doctrine. The fifth - that they say: the motion of light is upward and the motion of darkness is downward, then they affirmed mixture despite their claim that light was above and darkness below, and when the higher moves upward and the lower moves downward, they increase distance between them, not mixture. Thus mixture occurs only by the higher moving down or the lower moving up, and all that is impossible according to them. So if they affirm mixture with this, they have contradicted themselves. The sixth - that they made the two principles opposites, because opposition (al-taḍād) according to them is in substances (al-jawāhir) not accidents (al-a‘rāḍ), for they do not affirm the existence of accidents, and they say: it is the nature of opposites to repel and separate. Then they affirmed mixture, which is harmony and proximity, without affirming any compelling force over them, but rather by themselves and their natures, and this is a manifest contradiction, and praise be to God for success.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage presents six arguments against the dualists, who believe in two eternal principles: light (good) and darkness (evil). Each objection aims to show that the dualists' own principles lead to contradictions when applied to their doctrine of mixture (imitizāj) between light and darkness. The second argument points out that mixture is something new coming from no prior material, yet the dualists deny creation from nothing. The third argues that if two separated principles mix, each would produce two contradictory acts (separation and mixture) from a single substance, which they deem impossible. The fourth notes that they attribute weakness and ignorance (evils) to light but power (good) to darkness, contradicting their own assignment of good to light. The fifth uses the claims about upward/downward motion to show mixture would require impossible movements. The sixth notes that they consider opposites inherently repellent, yet mixture implies harmony, which they claim without a compelling force. The author concludes each objection with 'thus they contradict themselves.'

التضاد (al-taḍād)
التنافر (al-tanāfur)
التباعد (al-tabāʿud)
الائتلاف (al-iʾtilāf)
التقارب (al-taqārub)
قهر قاهر (qahr qāhir)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What do the dualists say is the nature of opposites?
A) To attract and unify
B) To repel and separate
C) To mix peacefully
D) To produce a third substance

Key Takeaway
Dualists affirm mixture despite their own principle that opposites naturally repel, an evident contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The dualists claimed opposites repel, yet they accepted mixture without a cause. Are there contradictions in your own life—beliefs you hold that your actions deny? What would it take for you to honestly admit those contradictions and seek the Compelling Force that resolves them?
?
This argument exposes a logical flaw in denying a creator while trying to explain harmony. Where do you personally rely on a 'mixture without a cause'—expecting good outcomes from your efforts without acknowledging the One who brings them together?
?
Al-Nasafi ends with praise to God for exposing contradiction. When was the last time you thanked God for revealing a falsehood you were comfortable with? What comfortable contradiction will you ask God to expose in your heart today?

Dialectical Refutation of Dualist Contradictions
The author refutes dualists through a series of dialectical questions leading to inevitable contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses a series of logical questions to expose the internal contradictions in the dualist worldview.

Core Idea
Dialectical questioning forces dualists into self-contradiction at every turn.

This passage is a masterclass in dialectical argument. Instead of directly proving Islamic monotheism, the author engages dualists on their own terms, asking a series of carefully crafted questions that lead inevitably to contradiction. By the end, whatever answer they give, their position collapses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once to grasp the flow of the argument. Notice the rhythm of question and expected answer.
The passage uses conditional statements (if they say... then...).
2
Identify the first two questions
The argument begins by asking about the status of an opponent: is he truthful or false? Then, if false, is his religion good or evil? Trace the implications of each answer.
The dualist cannot consistently claim their own religion is true while calling others false.
3
Follow the chain to the substances
Next, the author links the believer of an evil religion to the substance of darkness. Then asks if that substance can believe the true religion. See how this leads to an impossible imposition (taklīf).
This step forces the dualist to assign both good and evil to their own principles.
4
Understand the final dilemma
The author concludes that both good and evil come from the dualist's own doctrines, so they cannot separate light and darkness as pure sources. Any answer contradicts their own premises.
The final question 'Are you from light or darkness?' is rhetorical, as they have already shown inconsistency.
5
Reflect on the dialectical method
Consider why this method is effective: it uses the opponent's own beliefs to generate contradictions, without imposing external assumptions.
This is a classic kalam technique known as ilzām (forcing a conclusion).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم : من خالفكم في النحلة واعتقد دينا غير دينكم، أمحق هو أم مبطل؟ فإن قالوا: محق، فقد أقروا بصحة مذهب خصمهم، وبطلان مذهب أنفسهم، وإن قالوا هو مبطل، قيل : أشر دينه الباطل أم خير؟ فإن قالوا: هو خير، فقد بَان عنادهم، وإن قالوا: هو شر ، قيل : من المعتقد لذلك أجوهر النور أم جوهر الظلمة ؟ فإن قالوا: جوهر النور ، فقد ناقضوا وتركوا مذهبهم، وإن قالوا: جوهر الظلمة، قيل : أيتصور منه أن يعتقد الدين الحق؟ فإن قالوا: نعم، فقد ناقضوا، وإن قالوا: لا، قيل لهم فلم تناظرون خصمكم؟ ولم تدعونه إلى دينكم؟ وذلك غير متصور منه فإذا هذا منكم تكليف ما ليس في وسع المكلف، ولا يتصور لموجوده البتة، وهذا منكم سفه، فوجد منكم على زعمكم اعتقاد الحق وهو خير، وتكليف ما لا يتصور لوجوده وهو شر ، فجاء منكم الخير والشر، فمن جوهر النور أنتم أم من جوهر الظلمة؟ فبأي شيء أجابوا فقد ناقضوا وتركوا مذهبهم.
Then it is said to them: 'Whoever opposes you in sect and believes a religion other than your religion, is he truthful or false?' If they say: 'Truthful,' they have admitted the correctness of their opponent's doctrine and the falsity of their own doctrine. If they say: 'False,' it is said: 'Is his false religion evil or good?' If they say: 'Good,' their obstinacy becomes clear. If they say: 'Evil,' it is said: 'Who is the believer of that? Is it a substance of light or a substance of darkness?' If they say: 'Substance of light,' they contradict and abandon their doctrine. If they say: 'Substance of darkness,' it is said: 'Is it conceivable for it to believe the true religion?' If they say: 'Yes,' they contradict. If they say: 'No,' it is said to them: 'Then why do you argue with your opponent and call him to your religion, when that is not conceivable from him? So this from you is an imposition (taklīf) beyond the capacity of the obligated one, and it is not conceivable for its existence at all, and this from you is folly. Thus there came from you, according to your claim, belief in truth which is good, and imposition of what is not conceivable for its existence which is evil. So good and evil came from you. Are you from the substance of light or from the substance of darkness?' Whatever they answer, they contradict and abandon their doctrine.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical refutation. The author poses a series of questions to the dualists, forcing them into contradictions. Starting with an opponent of their religion, they are asked if that person is truthful (muḥiq) or false (mubṭil). Either answer leads to a problem: if truthful, they admit their own falsity; if false, they then must say whether that false religion is good or evil. If good, they contradict their own classification; if evil, then the believer of that evil must be from the substance of darkness (since darkness is the source of evil). But then they are asked if that substance can believe the true religion: if yes, contradiction; if no, then why do they invite such a person? That would be an impossible imposition (taklīf mā lā yuṭāq), which is evil, so both good and evil come from them, undermining their dualistic separation. The conclusion is that whatever they answer, they contradict themselves.

Key Terms
محق (muḥiq)
مبطل (mubṭil)
تكليف (taklīf)
النحلة (al-niḥla)
جوهر النور (jawhar al-nūr)
جوهر الظلمة (jawhar al-ẓulma)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The dialectical questions are merely rhetorical and do not constitute a logical refutation.
Correction: Each question forces the dualist to choose between premises that lead to a logical contradiction, demonstrating the internal inconsistency of their worldview.

Checkpoint
If the dualist says the opponent's religion is evil, and then says the believer of that evil is from the substance of darkness, what is the next question asked?
A) Can darkness bring about good?
B) Can the substance of darkness believe the true religion?
C) Why do you argue with him if he is from darkness?
D) Is the substance of light good or evil?

Key Takeaway
The author demonstrates that dualism leads to self-contradiction and that the concepts of good and evil cannot be attributed to separate substances without absurdity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held a belief that, when followed consistently, forced you into a contradiction? This passage shows that dualism cannot stand logical scrutiny. Are you willing to abandon any contradiction in your own faith, no matter how comfortable it has become?
?
The dualists here are cornered by their own logic. In your life, are there areas where you separate your belief from your action—claiming to follow truth while living as if it doesn't matter? This lesson exposes that such separation is unsustainable. What one specific inconsistency will you confront today?
?
The author's method is relentless because truth cannot compromise with falsehood. When you engage with others about your faith, do you seek to win an argument or to submit to the truth? Will you pray for sincerity and humility before your next conversation about what you believe?

Dialectical Refutation: Transition Between Religions
The author questions dualists about observed conversions between religions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses empirical observation of religious conversions to refute the dualist theory of two separate substances.

Core Idea
Observed conversions force dualists to admit a single substance can hold both truth and falsehood.

This passage presents a sharp dialectical challenge to the Dualist position. The author uses a simple question about observed conversions to expose a contradiction in their fundamental division of substances. By forcing the Dualists to choose between denying reality or accepting a contradiction, the argument effectively undermines their core doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: a question followed by two possible answers, each leading to a different conclusion.
The Arabic uses a conditional structure: 'If they say... then...'
2
Identify the two possible responses
The author presents two possible answers from the dualists: 'No' (they have not seen any conversion) or 'Yes' (they have). Consider the implications of each.
The 'No' response is dismissed as stubborn denial of observable facts. The 'Yes' response is used to build the contradiction.
3
Understand the logical trap
If the dualists say 'Yes', they must accept that a single substance (a person) can hold both true belief (good) and false belief (evil). This contradicts their core doctrine that good and evil come from two separate substances.
The argument relies on empirical observation—it is not merely theoretical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقال لهم هل رأيتم من انتقل من مذهبكم إلى غير مذهبكم وعلى القلب؟ فإن قالوا: لا، فقد كابروا وأنكروا المحسوس، وإن قالوا: نعم، فقد جوزوا من جوهر واحد اعتقاد الحق والباطل والحق خير و الباطل شر، وهذا منهم ترك لمذهبهم، والله الموفق.
And it is said to them: 'Have you seen anyone who transferred from your doctrine to another doctrine, and vice versa?' If they say: 'No,' they have been stubborn and denied the observable. If they say: 'Yes,' they have permitted from a single substance the belief of truth and falsehood, while truth is good and falsehood is evil. And this from them is abandonment of their doctrine. And God is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This short passage presents another dialectical argument. The author asks whether the dualists have observed people converting from their religion to another, and vice versa. If they deny it, they are simply ignoring empirical reality. If they admit it, then they must accept that a single substance (jawhar wāḥid) can hold both true belief (which is good) and false belief (which is evil). This contradicts their fundamental division of substances into light (good) and darkness (evil), since a single substance now produces both. The author concludes that this is an abandonment of their doctrine.

Key Terms
جوهر واحد (jawhar wāḥid)
الحق (al-ḥaqq)
الباطل (al-bāṭil)
الانتقال (al-intiqāl)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument is purely theoretical and does not rely on empirical observation.
Correction: The argument explicitly asks about observed conversions ('هل رأيتم...'), grounding it in empirical, observable reality. It is an empirical refutation, not merely a logical one.

Checkpoint
What does the second option ('Yes') force the dualists to admit about a single substance?
A) It can only believe truth.
B) It can only believe falsehood.
C) It can believe both truth and falsehood.
D) It cannot change its belief.

Key Takeaway
By observing religious conversions, the author shows that a single substance can embody both truth and falsehood, contradicting the dualist claim of two separate substances for good and evil.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The dualists were faced with a choice: deny observable reality or abandon their doctrine. When your own deeply held beliefs are challenged by clear evidence, are you willing to submit to the truth, or will you turn away? What would it cost you to change?
?
This passage shows that a single person can hold both truth and falsehood at different times. Have you ever been certain about something, only later to realize you were wrong? What does that say about your own need for humility and constant re-evaluation of your convictions?
?
The author used empirical observation to dismantle a false worldview. Are you actively examining your own beliefs against observable reality, or do you cling to them out of habit or comfort? What would it take for you to honestly question one of your core assumptions today?

Dialectical Refutation: Apology After Harm
Al-Nasafi begins a dialectical question about harm and apology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi introduces a dialectical scenario involving harm and apology to challenge dualist views on repentance and moral consistency.

Core Idea
Can dualism account for sincere repentance? Al-Nasafi's argument begins with a question.

In this fragment, Al-Nasafi presents a vivid hypothetical: a person harms another and then apologizes, confessing guilt. This scenario sets up a moral challenge to the dualist framework. Though the argument is cut off, the setup itself reveals a key point of tension. We will explore the opening of this argument and its likely direction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note that the passage ends mid-sentence with 'فإن'.
The passage is incomplete; the argument was intended to continue.
2
Identify the rhetorical structure
Notice that the author addresses the dualists directly with a rhetorical question: 'Have you seen anyone...' This is a common dialectical technique to draw the opponent into a concession.
3
Analyze the scenario's implications
Consider why this scenario of harm followed by apology is problematic for a dualist worldview that posits two eternal substances (good and evil). How can a person who did evil later repent? Does repentance imply a change in substance?
The incomplete argument likely aimed to show inconsistency.
4
Acknowledge the limitation
Recognize that the argument is cut off. We only have the premise. Reflect on what kind of conclusion might follow from 'فإن' (for if).
The next page would contain the continuation.

Source Text

The 'فإن' (for if) indicates that a follow-up question or conclusion was intended, likely leading to another contradiction in the dualist system, perhaps concerning the attribution of good and evil to the same substance or the possibility of repentance. Since the passage is incomplete, we can only describe its opening. The author is building a case that the dualist framework cannot account for such moral behavior consistently.

?

Refuting Dualism: The Chapter of Excuse
Imam al-Nasafi refutes dualist belief using the chapter of excuse argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the 'chapter of excuse' argument forces Manichaean dualists into a logical contradiction that demolishes their system.

Core Idea
Dualism cannot explain injustice without self-contradiction.

Imam al-Nasafi now deploys a powerful dialectical tool against Manichaean dualists. Their system posits two eternal principles: light (good) and darkness (evil). But what happens when we ask about the origin of injustice? The argument, known as the 'chapter of excuse', traps the dualist in a dilemma: whichever substance they point to, they violate their own foundational principles. Let's follow the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Set up the dilemma
Read the passage carefully. Notice how the argument begins by forcing the dualist to either deny injustice (stubbornness) or affirm it. If they affirm it, the real questioning starts.
2
Trace the first horn
If the dualist says injustice comes from light, then light would cause injustice, pain, and injury — contradicting the principle that light is wholly good.
3
Trace the second horn
If they say injustice comes from darkness, then consider the statement 'You have wronged me and I repent to you'. If that statement comes from light, light has lied (since it didn't wrong anyone). If from darkness, darkness has spoken truth — meaning good comes from darkness.
This is the key contradiction.
4
Recognize the chapter of excuse
The argument is called 'chapter of excuse' because it leaves the dualist no coherent excuse. Their entire system collapses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا: لا، فقد عاندوا وكابروا، وإن قالوا: نعم، قيل لهم من الجوهر الذي وجدت منه تلك الجناية أجوهر النور أم جوهر الظلمة ؟ فإن قالوا: جوهر النور، فقد أجازوا منه الظلم والجناية والإيلام والإيجاع، وهذا خلاف أصولهم. وإن قالوا: هو جوهر الظلمة، قيل : من الذي قال: ظلمت عليك وتبت إليك أجوهر النور هو أم جوهر الظلمة ؟ فإن قالوا: هو جوهر النور، فقد كذب، لأنه لم يظلم ولم يجن عليه، فإذا قال ظلمت وجنيت عليك، فقد كذب. وإن قالوا: هو جوهر الظلمة فقد صدق، لأنه أخبر أنه ظلمة وجنى عليه، وكان الأمر على ما أخبر والصدق خير، فقد وجد من جوهر الظلمة الخير وهذا الفصل يسمى فصل الاعتذار، وفيه هدم أصولهم وإبطال قواعد دينهم، والله الموفق.
They said: No, for they obstinately persisted and denied. And if they say: Yes, it is said to them: From which substance did that injury come? Is it the substance of light or the substance of darkness? If they say: The substance of light, then they have permitted from it injustice, injury, causing pain, and causing suffering, and this contradicts their principles. And if they say: It is the substance of darkness, it is said: Who said: 'You have wronged me and I repent to you'? Is it the substance of light or the substance of darkness? If they say: It is the substance of light, then he has lied, because it did not wrong nor was it wronged, so if he says 'I have wronged and been wronged', he has lied. And if they say: It is the substance of darkness, then he has told the truth, because he informed that it is darkness and was wronged, and the matter was as he informed, and truth is better, so good has been found from the substance of darkness. And this chapter is called the chapter of excuse, and in it is the demolition of their principles and the invalidation of the foundations of their religion. And God is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical refutation of Manichaean dualists. The argument proceeds by asking about the origin of injustice. If the dualist denies injustice occurs, he is stubborn. If he affirms it, he must attribute it to either light or darkness. Attributing it to light contradicts their principle that light is wholly good. Attributing it to darkness leads to a problem: the person who says 'You have wronged me and I repent to you' — if they attribute this statement to light, then light has lied; if to darkness, then darkness has spoken truth, meaning good comes from darkness. Thus caught in contradiction, the dualist's position collapses. This argument is called the chapter of excuse (fasl al-‘itidhār), which demolishes their foundations.

Key Terms
فصل الاعتذار
الجوهر
النور
الظلمة
الظلم
الجناية
الإيلام
الإيجاع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think dualism has a consistent explanation for good and evil.
Correction: This argument shows that dualism cannot attribute injustice to either principle without contradiction.

Checkpoint
What is the outcome of the 'chapter of excuse' argument for the dualists?
A) It proves that light is the source of all good and evil.
B) It shows that darkness can also produce good, saving their view.
C) It forces a contradiction: if injustice comes from light, light is evil; if from darkness, then good comes from darkness.
D) It proves that the third mediator resolves the problem.

Key Takeaway
The 'chapter of excuse' forces dualists into an inescapable contradiction, showing that no coherent system based on two opposite principles can explain the existence of injustice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just seen that dualists cannot attribute evil to a separate principle without contradiction. When you sin, do you sometimes tell yourself 'it was my circumstances' or 'my upbringing' — as if there is a 'darkness' outside you? Will you instead own your wrong and repent, knowing that truth is good?
?
The dualist who claims light is the speaker and says 'You wronged me' is lying. Have you ever played the victim while hiding your own fault? Can you let go of that pose and speak truth even if it costs your pride?
?
Imam al-Nasafi forces the opponent to admit that truth is good no matter the source. In your life, are you willing to accept hard truths about yourself (your weaknesses, sins) even when they come from an unexpected source? Or do you dismiss them because the messenger is flawed?
